When you signed those six new states into law, you thought not of the snowcapped mountains and the windswept plains. PALMER WINS AFTER HARD-FOUGHT CAMPAIGN

My life is like the prints which feet


Have left on Tampa's desert strand;


You aren't watching the results anymore. You know what they say. You know what they mean. You shudder in your chair, in your room, in the Executive Mansion. How warm it felt when you were master of this house. How cold it feels, now that you are only a guest.

Soon as the rising tide shall beat,


All trace will vanish from the sand;


The beautiful lie eats up the ugly truth. The heroes of 'reform' win their long-awaited victory over the Stalwart. It didn't matter how much you tried to play by the rules in this election. You sacrificed your edge to please the mewling animals that were always going to call you crooked anyway. Defend yourself, in your newfound spare time, if you want. Cling to the side of the mountain in the cold dark, fighting the frigid winds that blast you from every direction, thoughtlessly, endlessly. Too many enemies, too many daggers in the back. Too few friends to survive. Maybe you, in four short years, made a difference. But just four years of work, against the crashing tides of centuries of history. How long until all of it is washed away?

Yet, as if grieving to efface


All vestige of the human race,


None of them understand power. To work to make yourself worthy of bearing it, to wield it, to guard it, to suffer beneath its burden. To learn to hold it so close it burns your skin. To love it and hate it, so that America, at the close of day, ticks over not into another today, but into tomorrow. When they curse your name, when they burn your effigy, when they dance and sing in the streets when they hear of your downfall, do they hear the sound of something dying? Would they care even if they could?

On that lone shore loud moans the sea,


But none, alas, shall mourn for me.


-- 'The Lament of the Captive' by Richard Henry Wilde
